     <p><b>Northwestern University</b> (<b>NU</b>) is a private research university with campuses in <a href="/wiki/Evanston,_Illinois" title="Evanston, Illinois">Evanston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> in <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, United States. Northwestern has 12 undergraduate, graduate, and professional schools offering 124 undergraduate degrees and 145 graduate and professional degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-Ugrad_program_list_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ugrad_program_list-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Grad_program_list_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grad_program_list-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Northwestern was founded in 1851 by <a href="/wiki/John_Evans_(governor)" title="John Evans (governor)">John Evans</a>, for whom Evanston is named, and eight other lawyers, businessmen and Methodist leaders to serve the people of a region that had once been known as the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territory" title="Northwest Territory">Northwest Territory</a>. Instruction began in 1855; women were admitted in 1869. Today, the main campus is a 240-acre (97&nbsp;ha) parcel in Evanston, along the shores of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Michigan" title="Lake Michigan">Lake Michigan</a>. The university's <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Law" title="Northwestern University School of Law">law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Feinberg_School_of_Medicine" title="Feinberg School of Medicine">medical schools</a> are located on a 25-acre (10&nbsp;ha) campus in Chicago's <a href="/wiki/Streeterville" title="Streeterville">Streeterville</a> neighborhood. In 2008, the University opened a campus in <a href="/wiki/Education_City" title="Education City">Education City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> with programs in journalism and communication. In academic year 2010-2011, Northwestern enrolled 8,397 undergraduate and 7,870 graduate and professional students.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS-B_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-B-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Northwestern has one of the largest university endowments in the United States, valued at $7.1 billion in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-nacubo_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nacubo-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> One of only 62 institutions elected to the Association of American Universities (1917), Northwestern was awarded more than $500 million in research grants in 2010?2011, placing it in the first tier of the major research universities in the United States by the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="Center for Measuring University Performance">Center for Measuring University Performance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AAU_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AAU-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Its schools of management, engineering, and communication, for example, are among the most academically productive in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-FSPI_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FSPI-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Northwestern is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> and remains the only private university in the conference. The <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats" title="Northwestern Wildcats">Northwestern Wildcats</a> compete in 19 intercollegiate sports in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a>.</p>

            <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Undergraduate_housing"><span class="tocnumber">5.6</span> <span class="toctext">Undergraduate housing</span></a></li> 
           </ul> </li> 
          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Athletics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Athletics</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#People"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">People</span></a>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Northwestern_University" title="History of Northwestern University">History of Northwestern University</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The foundation of Northwestern University is traceable to a meeting on May 31, 1850 of nine prominent Chicago businessmen, Methodist leaders and attorneys who had formed the idea of establishing a university to serve what had once been known as the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territory" title="Northwest Territory">Northwest Territory</a>. On January 28, 1851, the <a href="/wiki/Illinois_General_Assembly" title="Illinois General Assembly">Illinois General Assembly</a> granted a charter to the <i>Trustees of the North-Western University</i>, making it the first chartered university in Illinois.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Charter_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charter-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="ref_anone"><a href="#endnote_anone">[a]</a></sup> The school's nine founders, all of whom were Methodists (three of them <a href="/wiki/Elder_(Methodism)" title="Elder (Methodism)">ministers</a>), knelt in <a href="/wiki/Prayer_in_Christianity" title="Prayer in Christianity" class="mw-redirect">prayer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christian_worship" title="Christian worship">worship</a> before launching their first organizational meeting.<sup id="cite_ref-Northwestern_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Northwestern-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Although they affiliated the university with the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="Methodist Episcopal Church">Methodist Episcopal Church</a>, they were committed to <a href="/wiki/Non-sectarian" title="Non-sectarian" class="mw-redirect">non-sectarian</a> admissions, believing that Northwestern should serve all people in the newly developing territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Planning_a_university_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Planning_a_university-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>John Evans, for whom Evanston is named, bought 379 acres (153&nbsp;ha) of land along Lake Michigan in 1853, and Philo Judson developed plans for what would become the city of <a href="/wiki/Evanston,_Illinois" title="Evanston, Illinois">Evanston</a>. The first building, <a href="/wiki/Old_College,_Northwestern_University" title="Old College, Northwestern University" class="mw-redirect">Old College</a>, opened on November 5, 1855.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> To raise funds for construction, Northwestern sold $100 &quot;perpetual scholarships&quot; entitling the purchaser and his heirs to free tuition.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Perpetual_scholarships_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Perpetual_scholarships-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1873 the <a href="/wiki/Evanston_College_for_Ladies" title="Evanston College for Ladies">Evanston College for Ladies</a> merged with Northwestern, and <a href="/wiki/Frances_Willard_(suffragist)" title="Frances Willard (suffragist)">Frances Willard</a>, who later gained fame as a <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage" title="Women's suffrage">suffragette</a> and as one of the founders of the Woman's Christian Temperance Union (WCTU), became the school's first dean of women. Willard Residential College (1938) is named in her honor. Northwestern admitted its first women students in 1869, and the first woman was graduated in 1874.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Northwestern fielded its first intercollegiate football team in 1882, later becoming a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>. In the 1870s and 1880s, Northwestern affiliated itself with already existing schools of law, medicine, and dentistry in Chicago. As the university increased in wealth and distinction, and enrollments grew, these professional schools were integrated with the undergraduate college in Evanston; the result was a modern research university combining professional, graduate, and undergraduate programs, which gave equal weight to teaching and research.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> invited Northwestern to become a member in 1917.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Deering_front.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Deering_front.jpg/220px-Deering_front.jpg" width="220" height="82" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Deering_front.jpg/330px-Deering_front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Deering_front.jpg/440px-Deering_front.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Deering_front.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Deering Library (1933)
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Under <a href="/wiki/Walter_Dill_Scott" title="Walter Dill Scott">Walter Dill Scott</a>'s presidency from 1920 to 1939, Northwestern began construction of an integrated campus in Chicago designed by <a href="/wiki/James_Gamble_Rogers" title="James Gamble Rogers">James Gamble Rogers</a> to house the professional schools; established the <a href="/wiki/Kellogg_School_of_Management" title="Kellogg School of Management">Kellogg School of Management</a>; and built several prominent buildings on the Evanston campus, <a href="/wiki/Dyche_Stadium" title="Dyche Stadium" class="mw-redirect">Dyche Stadium</a> (now named Ryan Field) and <a href="/wiki/Deering_Library" title="Deering Library">Deering Library</a> among others. In 1933, a proposal to merge Northwestern with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a> was considered but rejected.<sup id="cite_ref-Barnes_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barnes-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UChicago_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UChicago-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Northwestern played host to the first-ever <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship</a> game in 1939 in the original <a href="/wiki/Patten_Gymnasium" title="Patten Gymnasium">Patten Gymnasium</a>, later demolished and relocated farther north to make room for the <a href="/wiki/Technological_Institute" title="Technological Institute" class="mw-redirect">Technological Institute</a>.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg/220px-University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg/330px-University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg/440px-University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:University_Hall_Northwestern.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> University Hall (1869), the second building constructed on campus, and the oldest building still standing.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Like other American research universities, Northwestern was transformed by <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. <a href="/wiki/Franklyn_B._Snyder" title="Franklyn B. Snyder" class="mw-redirect">Franklyn B. Snyder</a> led the university from 1939 to 1949, when nearly 50,000 military officers and personnel were trained on the Evanston and Chicago campuses. After the war, surging enrollments under the <a href="/wiki/G.I._Bill" title="G.I. Bill">G.I. Bill</a> drove drastic expansion of both campuses. In 1948 prominent anthropologist <a href="/wiki/Melville_J._Herskovits" title="Melville J. Herskovits">Melville J. Herskovits</a> founded the Program of <a href="/wiki/African_Studies" title="African Studies" class="mw-redirect">African Studies</a> at Northwestern, the first center of its kind at an American academic institution.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/J._Roscoe_Miller" title="J. Roscoe Miller">J. Roscoe Miller</a>'s tenure as president from 1949 to 1970 was responsible for the expansion of the Evanston campus, with the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Lakefill" title="Lakefill" class="mw-redirect">lakefill</a> on Lake Michigan, growth of the faculty and new academic programs, as well as polarizing Vietnam-era student protests. In 1978, the first and second <a href="/wiki/Unabomber" title="Unabomber" class="mw-redirect">Unabomber</a> attacks occurred at Northwestern University.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Relations between Evanston and Northwestern were strained throughout much of the post-war era because of episodes of disruptive student activism,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> disputes over municipal zoning, building codes, and law enforcement,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as restrictions on the sale of alcohol near campus until 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dry_campus_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dry_campus-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Northwestern's exemption from state and municipal property tax obligations under its original charter has historically been a source of <a href="/wiki/Town_and_gown" title="Town and gown">town and gown</a> tension.</p> 
     <p>Though government support for universities declined in the 1970s and 1980s, President <a href="/wiki/Arnold_R._Weber" title="Arnold R. Weber">Arnold R. Weber</a> was able to stabilize university finances, leading to a revitalization of the campuses. As admissions to colleges and universities grew increasingly competitive in the 1990s and 2000s, President <a href="/wiki/Henry_S._Bienen" title="Henry S. Bienen" class="mw-redirect">Henry S. Bienen</a>'s tenure saw a notable increase in the number and quality of undergraduate applicants, continued expansion of the facilities and faculty, and renewed athletic competitiveness. In 1999, Northwestern student journalists uncovered information exonerating Illinois death row inmate <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Porter" title="Anthony Porter">Anthony Porter</a> two days before his scheduled execution, and the Innocence Project has since exonerated 10 more men.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> On January 11, 2003, in a speech at Northwestern School of Law's Lincoln Hall, then <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Illinois" title="Governor of Illinois">Governor of Illinois</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Ryan" title="George Ryan">George Ryan</a> announced that he would <a href="/wiki/Commutation_of_sentence" title="Commutation of sentence">commute</a> the sentences of more than 150 <a href="/wiki/Death_row" title="Death row">death row</a> inmates.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> phrase on Northwestern's seal, <i>Quaecumque sunt vera</i> (Whatsoever things are true) is drawn from the Epistle of Paul to the Philippians 4:8, while the Greek phrase inscribed on the pages of an open book is taken from the Gospel of John 1:14: <i>? ????? ?????? ??????? ??? ????????</i> (The Word full of grace and truth).<sup id="cite_ref-Faith_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faith-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Seal_history_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seal_history-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Purple" title="Purple">Purple</a> became Northwestern's official color in 1892,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> replacing <a href="/wiki/Black" title="Black">black</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> after a university committee concluded that too many other universities had used these colors. Today, Northwestern's official color is purple, although white is something of an official color as well, being mentioned in both the university's earliest song, <i>Alma Mater</i> (1907) (&quot;Hail to purple, hail to white&quot;) and in many university guidelines.<sup id="cite_ref-purple_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-purple-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-School_colors_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-School_colors-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_buildings" title="List of Northwestern University buildings">List of Northwestern University buildings</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evanston">Evanston</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Evanston">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg/220px-Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg" width="220" height="80" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg/330px-Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg/440px-Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_University_Evanston_campus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Northwestern's Evanston campus is located on 
        <a href="/wiki/Lake_Michigan" title="Lake Michigan">Lake Michigan</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Northwestern's Evanston campus, where the undergraduate schools, the Graduate School, and the Kellogg School of Management are located, runs north-south from Lincoln Avenue to Clark Street west of Lake Michigan along <a href="/wiki/Sheridan_Road" title="Sheridan Road">Sheridan Road</a>. North and South Campuses have noticeably different atmospheres, owing to the predominance of Science and Athletics in the one and Humanities and Arts in the other. North Campus is home to the <a href="/wiki/Fraternity_and_sorority_houses" title="Fraternity and sorority houses" class="mw-redirect">fraternity</a> <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">quads</a>, the Henry Crown Sports Pavilion and Norris Aquatics Center and other athletic facilities, the <a href="/wiki/Technological_Institute" title="Technological Institute" class="mw-redirect">Technological Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dearborn_Observatory" title="Dearborn Observatory">Dearborn Observatory</a>, and other science-related buildings including Patrick G. and Shirley W. Ryan Hall for Nanofabrication and Molecular Self-Assembly, and the Ford Motor Company Engineering Design Center. South Campus is home to the University's humanities buildings, <a href="/wiki/Pick-Staiger_Concert_Hall" title="Pick-Staiger Concert Hall">Pick-Staiger Concert Hall</a> and other music buildings, the <a href="/wiki/Mary_and_Leigh_Block_Museum_of_Art" title="Mary and Leigh Block Museum of Art">Mary and Leigh Block Museum of Art</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Fraternity_and_sorority_houses" title="Fraternity and sorority houses" class="mw-redirect">sorority</a> quads. In the 1960s, the University created an additional 84 acres (34.0&nbsp;ha) by means of a lakefill in Lake Michigan. Among some of the buildings located on these broad new acres are University Library, <a href="/wiki/Norris_University_Center" title="Norris University Center">Norris University Center</a> (the student union), and <a href="/wiki/Pick-Staiger_Concert_Hall" title="Pick-Staiger Concert Hall">Pick-Staiger Concert Hall</a>.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Transit_Authority" title="Chicago Transit Authority">Chicago Transit Authority</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Chicago_%27L%27" title="Chicago 'L'">elevated train</a> running through Evanston is called the <a href="/wiki/Purple_Line_(Chicago_Transit_Authority)" title="Purple Line (Chicago Transit Authority)" class="mw-redirect">Purple Line</a>, taking its name from Northwestern's school color. The <a href="/wiki/Foster_(CTA)" title="Foster (CTA)" class="mw-redirect">Foster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Davis_(CTA)" title="Davis (CTA)" class="mw-redirect">Davis</a> stations are within walking distance of the southern end of the campus, while the <a href="/wiki/Noyes_(CTA)" title="Noyes (CTA)" class="mw-redirect">Noyes</a> station is close to the northern end of the campus. The <a href="/wiki/Central_(CTA_Purple_Line)" title="Central (CTA Purple Line)" class="mw-redirect">Central</a> station is close to <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Field_(stadium)" title="Ryan Field (stadium)">Ryan Field</a>, Northwestern's football stadium. The <a href="/wiki/Evanston_Davis_Street_(Metra)" title="Evanston Davis Street (Metra)">Evanston Davis Street</a> <a href="/wiki/Metra" title="Metra">Metra</a> station serves the Northwestern campus in downtown Evanston and the <a href="/wiki/Evanston_Central_Street_(Metra)" title="Evanston Central Street (Metra)">Evanston Central Street</a> Metra station is near Ryan Field. Pace Suburban Bus Service and the CTA have several bus routes that run through or near the Evanston campus.</p> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:808px;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner"> 
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG" class="image" title="Panorama of Northwestern University in Evanston"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG/800px-Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG" width="800" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG/1200px-Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG/1600px-Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG 2x" /></a>
       </div> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_University_lakefill_panorama.PNG" title="Enlarge"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6b/Magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" /></a>
        </div> 
        <center>
         <i>Panorama of Northwestern University in Evanston</i>
        </center> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chicago">Chicago</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Chicago">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ward_Building_060527.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ward_Building_060527.jpg/220px-Ward_Building_060527.jpg" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ward_Building_060527.jpg/330px-Ward_Building_060527.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Ward_Building_060527.jpg/440px-Ward_Building_060527.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ward_Building_060527.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Montgomery Ward Memorial Building (1927) at Northwestern's Feinberg School of Medicine in Chicago, America's first academic skyscraper.
        <sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_1949_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_1949-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Northwestern's Chicago campus is located in the city's <a href="/wiki/Streeterville" title="Streeterville">Streeterville</a> neighborhood. The Chicago campus is home to the <a href="/wiki/Feinberg_School_of_Medicine" title="Feinberg School of Medicine">medical school</a> and affiliated hospitals, the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Law" title="Northwestern University School of Law">law school</a>, the part-time MBA program, and the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Continuing_Studies" title="Northwestern University School of Continuing Studies">School of Continuing Studies</a>, which offers evening and weekend courses for working adults. Northwestern's professional schools and affiliated hospitals are about four blocks east of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_(CTA_Red_Line)" title="Chicago (CTA Red Line)" class="mw-redirect">Chicago</a> station on the CTA <a href="/wiki/Red_Line_(Chicago_Transit_Authority)" title="Red Line (Chicago Transit Authority)" class="mw-redirect">Red Line</a>. The Chicago campus is also served by CTA bus routes.</p> 
     <p>Founded at various times in the university's history, the professional schools originally were scattered throughout Chicago.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_Campus_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago_Campus-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> In connection with a 1917 master plan for a central Chicago campus and President Walter D. Scott's capital campaign, 8.5 acres (3.44&nbsp;ha) of land were purchased at the corner of <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Avenue" title="Chicago Avenue">Chicago Avenue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Shore_Drive" title="Lake Shore Drive">Lake Shore Drive</a> for $1.5 million in 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_Campus_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago_Campus-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_Campus_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago_Campus-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The architect <a href="/wiki/James_Gamble_Rogers" title="James Gamble Rogers">James Gamble Rogers</a> was commissioned to create a master plan for the principal buildings on the new campus which he designed in <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_gothic" title="Collegiate gothic" class="mw-redirect">collegiate gothic</a> style. In 1923, Mrs. <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_Ward" title="Montgomery Ward">Montgomery Ward</a> donated $8 million to the campaign to finance the construction of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Montgomery_Ward_Memorial_Building&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Montgomery Ward Memorial Building (page does not exist)">Montgomery Ward Memorial Building</a> which would house the medical and dental schools and to create endowments for faculty chairs, research grants, scholarships, and building maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-Montgomery_Ward_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Montgomery_Ward-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The building would become the first university skyscraper in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Timeline_1949_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timeline_1949-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to the Ward Building, Rogers designed <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_buildings#Wieboldt_Hall" title="List of Northwestern University buildings">Wieboldt Hall</a> to house facilities for the School of Commerce<sup id="cite_ref-Wieboldt_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wieboldt-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_buildings#Levy_Mayer_Hall" title="List of Northwestern University buildings">Levy Mayer Hall</a> to house the School of Law.<sup id="cite_ref-Levy_Mayer_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levy_Mayer-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> The new campus comprising these three new buildings was dedicated during a two-day ceremony in June 1927. The Chicago campus continued to expand with the addition of <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_buildings#Thorn_Hall" title="List of Northwestern University buildings">Thorn Hall</a> in 1931 and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_buildings#Abbott_Hall" title="List of Northwestern University buildings">Abbott Hall</a> in 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_Campus_36-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago_Campus-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Abbott_Hall_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abbott_Hall-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite_Campus_in_Qatar">Satellite Campus in Qatar</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Satellite Campus in Qatar">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In Fall 2008, Northwestern opened a campus in <a href="/wiki/Education_City" title="Education City">Education City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, joining five other American universities: <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University" title="Texas A&amp;M University">Texas A&amp;M University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University" title="Virginia Commonwealth University">Virginia Commonwealth University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-meivy_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meivy-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Through the <a href="/wiki/Medill_School_of_Journalism" title="Medill School of Journalism">Medill School of Journalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Communication" title="Northwestern University School of Communication">School of Communication</a>, NU-Q offers <a href="/wiki/Bachelors_degree" title="Bachelors degree" class="mw-redirect">bachelors degrees</a> in journalism and communication respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Foundation_for_Education,_Science_and_Community_Development" title="Qatar Foundation for Education, Science and Community Development" class="mw-redirect">Qatar Foundation for Education, Science and Community Development</a> provided funding for construction and administrative costs as well as support to hire 50 to 60 faculty and staff, some of whom rotate between the Evanston and Qatar campuses.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In January 2009, the Green Power Partnership (GPP, sponsored by the EPA) listed Northwestern as one of the top 10 universities in the country in purchasing energy from renewable sources. The university matches 74 million kilowatt hours (kWh) of its annual energy use with Green-e Certified Renewable Energy Certificates (RECs). This green power commitment represents 30 percent of the university's total annual electricity use and places Northwestern in the EPA's Green Power Leadership Club. The 2010 Report by The Sustainable Endowments Institute awarded Northwestern a &quot;B-&quot; on its College Sustainability Report Card.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The Initiative for Sustainability and Energy at Northwestern (ISEN), supporting research, teaching and outreach in these themes, was launched in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Northwestern requires that all new buildings be <a href="/wiki/LEED-certified" title="LEED-certified" class="mw-redirect">LEED-certified</a>. Silverman Hall on the Evanston campus was awarded Gold LEED Certification in 2010; Wieboldt Hall on the Chicago campus was awarded Gold LEED Certification in 2007, and the Ford Motor Company Engineering Design Center on the Evanston campus was awarded Silver LEED Certification in 2006. New construction and renovation projects will be designed to provide at least a 20% improvement over energy code requirements where technically feasible.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also released at the beginning of the 2008?09 academic year the Evanston Campus Framework Plan, which outlines plans for future development of the Evanston Campus. The plan not only emphasizes the sustainable construction of buildings, but also discusses improving transportation by optimizing pedestrian and bicycle access.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Northwestern has had a comprehensive recycling program in place since 1990. Annually more than 1,500 tons are recycled at Northwestern, which represents 30% of the waste produced on campus. Additionally, all landscape waste at the university is composted.<sup id="cite_ref-Northwestern_University_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Northwestern_University-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization_and_administration">Organization and administration</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Organization and administration">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Northwestern is privately owned and is governed by an appointed <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Trustees" title="Board of Trustees" class="mw-redirect">Board of Trustees</a>. The board, composed of 70 members and as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> chaired by <a href="/wiki/William_A._Osborn" title="William A. Osborn">William A. Osborn</a> '69, delegates its power to an elected president to serve as the chief executive officer of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Northwestern has had <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_presidents" title="List of Northwestern University presidents">sixteen presidents in its history</a> (excluding interim presidents), the current president, <a href="/wiki/Morton_O._Schapiro" title="Morton O. Schapiro">Morton O. Schapiro</a>, an economist, having succeeded <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bienen" title="Henry Bienen">Henry Bienen</a> whose 14-year tenure ended on August 31, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> The president has a staff of vice presidents, directors, and other assistants for administrative, financial, faculty, and student matters.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Daniel_I._Linzer" title="Daniel I. Linzer">Daniel I. Linzer</a>, provost since September 2007, serves under the president as the chief academic officer of the university to whom the deans of every academic school, leaders of cross-disciplinary units, and chairs of the standing faculty committee report.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Associated Student Government consists of the elected representatives of the undergraduate students and the Graduate Student Association represents graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Northwestern University is composed of 12 schools and colleges. The faculty for each school consists of the dean of the school and the instructional faculty. Faculty are responsible for teaching, research, advising students, and serving on committees. Each school's admission requirements, degree requirements, courses of study, and disciplinary and degree recommendations are determined by the voting members of that school's faculty (assistant professor and above).<sup id="cite_ref-Faculty_handbook_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faculty_handbook-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Northwestern's endowment was $7.1 billion as of June 30, 2012, the tenth largest among US and Canadian universities.<sup id="cite_ref-nacubo_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nacubo-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2003, Northwestern finished a five-year capital campaign that raised $1.55 billion, $550 million more than its goal. In 2007, the university sold its royalty interest in the pain relief drug <a href="/wiki/Lyrica" title="Lyrica" class="mw-redirect">Lyrica</a> for $700 million, a drug developed at Northwestern by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Bruce_Silverman" title="Richard Bruce Silverman">Richard Bruce Silverman</a>, the John Evans Professor of Chemistry. This was the largest such sale in history,<sup id="cite_ref-Lyrica_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyrica-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> the proceeds of which were added to the endowment.<sup id="cite_ref-Financial_Report_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Financial_Report-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table style="border:1px solid #ddd; background:#fefefe; padding:3px; margin:0;"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr style="vertical-align:top; text-align:left;"> 
        <th style="width:475pt;"><span style="font-size:115%;">Undergraduate and Graduate Schools</span></th> 
        <th style="width:300pt;"><span style="font-size:115%;">Graduate and Professional</span></th> 
       </tr>

          <li><a href="/wiki/Bienen_School_of_Music" title="Bienen School of Music">Bienen School of Music</a> (1895)</li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/McCormick_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Science" title="McCormick School of Engineering and Applied Science" class="mw-redirect">McCormick School of Engineering and Applied Science</a> (1909)</li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Medill_School_of_Journalism" title="Medill School of Journalism">Medill School of Journalism</a> (1921)</li>

     </table> 
     <p>Northwestern University had a dental school from 1891 to May 31, 2001, when it closed.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <table class="infobox vcard" style="width: 22em"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <th colspan="2" class="n" style="text-align: center; font-size: 125%"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings" title="College and university rankings">University rankings</a></span></th>

        <td>27</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_THES_W_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_THES_W-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>19</td>
