     <p>Northwestern is a large, residential research university.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Accredited by the <a href="/wiki/North_Central_Association_of_Colleges_and_Schools" title="North Central Association of Colleges and Schools">North Central Association of Colleges and Schools</a> and the respective national professional organizations for chemistry, psychology, business, education, journalism, music, engineering, law, and medicine,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> the university offers 124 undergraduate programs and 145 graduate and professional programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Ugrad_program_list_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ugrad_program_list-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Grad_program_list_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grad_program_list-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> NU conferred 2,219 bachelors degrees, 2,971 masters degrees, 447 doctoral degrees, and 444 <a href="/wiki/Professional_degree" title="Professional degree" class="mw-redirect">professional degrees</a> in 2009?2010.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS-B_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-B-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The four-year, full-time undergraduate program comprises the majority of enrollments at the university and emphasizes instruction in the arts and sciences, plus the professions of engineering, journalism, communication, music, and education.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Although a foundation in the liberal arts and sciences is required in all majors, there is no required common core curriculum; individual degree requirements are set by the faculty of each school.<sup id="cite_ref-Faculty_handbook_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Faculty_handbook-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Northwestern's full-time undergraduate and graduate programs operate on an approximately 10-week <a href="/wiki/Academic_quarter_(year_division)" title="Academic quarter (year division)">academic quarter system</a> with the academic year beginning in late September and ending in early June. Undergraduates typically take 4 courses each quarter and 12 courses in an academic year and<sup id="cite_ref-Catalog_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalog-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> are required to complete at least 12 quarters on campus to graduate. Northwestern offers honors, accelerated, and joint degree programs in medicine, science, mathematics, engineering, and journalism.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The comprehensive doctoral graduate program has high coexistence with undergraduate programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Undergraduates with <a href="/wiki/Grade_point_average" title="Grade point average" class="mw-redirect">grade point averages</a> in the highest 3 percent of each graduating class are awarded degrees <i><a href="/wiki/Latin_honors" title="Latin honors">summa cum laude</a></i>, the next 5 percent <i>magna cum laude</i>, and the next 8 percent <i>cum laude</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Honors_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Honors-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Northwestern also has chapters of academic honor societies such as <a href="/wiki/Phi_Beta_Kappa" title="Phi Beta Kappa" class="mw-redirect">Phi Beta Kappa</a> (Alpha of Illinois), <a href="/wiki/Eta_Kappa_Nu" title="Eta Kappa Nu">Eta Kappa Nu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tau_Beta_Pi" title="Tau Beta Pi">Tau Beta Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lambda_Pi_Eta" title="Lambda Pi Eta">Lambda Pi Eta</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Honors_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Honors-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Sigma_Lambda" title="Alpha Sigma Lambda">Alpha Sigma Lambda</a> (Alpha Chapter).<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 1951, Northwestern has awarded 520 <a href="/wiki/Honorary_degrees" title="Honorary degrees" class="mw-redirect">honorary degrees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Undergraduate tuition for the 2012/13 school year is $61,240; this includes the basic tuition of $43,380, fees (health $200, etc.), room and board of $13,329 (less if commuting), books and supplies $1,842, personal expenses $1,890, transportation cost of $400.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalog-FinAid_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalog-FinAid-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Northwestern awards financial aid solely on the basis of need through loans, work-study, grants, and scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalog-FinAid_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalog-FinAid-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FinAid_FAQ_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FinAid_FAQ-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The University processed in excess of $472 million in financial aid for the 2009?2010 academic year. This included $265 million in institutional funds, with the remainder coming from federal and state governments and private organizations and individuals. Northwestern scholarship programs for undergraduate students support needy students from a variety of income and backgrounds. Approximately 44 percent of the June 2010 graduates had received federal and/or private loans for their undergraduate education, graduating with an average debt of $17,200.</p> 
     <p>Among the six undergraduate schools, 51.6% of undergraduate students are enrolled in the <a href="/wiki/Weinberg_College_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Weinberg College of Arts and Sciences">Weinberg College of Arts and Sciences</a>, 17.4% in the <a href="/wiki/McCormick_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Science" title="McCormick School of Engineering and Applied Science" class="mw-redirect">McCormick School of Engineering and Applied Science</a>, 13.7% in the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Communication" title="Northwestern University School of Communication">School of Communication</a>, 8.1% in the <a href="/wiki/Medill_School_of_Journalism" title="Medill School of Journalism">Medill School of Journalism</a>, 4.3% in the <a href="/wiki/Bienen_School_of_Music" title="Bienen School of Music">Bienen School of Music</a>, and 4.9% in the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Education" title="Northwestern University School of Education" class="mw-redirect">School of Education and Social Policy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Enrollments_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enrollments-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The five most commonly awarded undergraduate degrees are in economics, journalism, communication studies, psychology, and political science.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> While professional students are affiliated with their respective schools, full-time graduate academic degrees are primarily administered by the Graduate School.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Catalog-11_Schools_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalog-11_Schools-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> With 2,446 students enrolled in science, engineering, and health fields,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> the largest graduate programs by enrollment include chemistry, integrated biology, material sciences, electrical and computer engineering, neuroscience, and economics.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kellogg_School_of_Management" title="Kellogg School of Management">Kellogg School of Management</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Business_Administration" title="Master of Business Administration">MBA</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Law" title="Northwestern University School of Law">School of Law</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">JD</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Feinberg_School_of_Medicine" title="Feinberg School of Medicine">Feinberg School of Medicine</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">MD</a> are the three largest <a href="/wiki/First_professional_degree" title="First professional degree">professional degree</a> programs by enrollment.<sup id="cite_ref-Enrollments_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enrollments-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries_and_museums">Libraries and museums</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Libraries and museums">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/de/University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg/220px-University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/de/University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg/330px-University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/de/University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg/440px-University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:University_Library_at_Northwestern.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> University Library (1970) in 
        <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">Brutalist</a> style.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Northwestern library system consists of four libraries on the Evanston campus including the central <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Library" title="Northwestern University Library">University Library</a>, three libraries on the Chicago campus, and the library affiliated with Garrett-Evangelical Theological Seminary.<sup id="cite_ref-Library_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> University Library contains over 4.9 million volumes, 4.6 million microforms, and almost 99,000 periodicals making it (by volume) the 30th-largest university library in North America and the 10th-largest library among private universities.<sup id="cite_ref-Library_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Library_Stats_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library_Stats-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable collections in the library system include the Melville J. Herskovits Library of African Studies, one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Africana_studies" title="Africana studies">Africana</a> collections in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> an extensive collection of early edition printed music and manuscripts as well as late-modern works, and an art collection noted for its 19th and 20th-century <a href="/wiki/Western_art_history" title="Western art history" class="mw-redirect">Western art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Architecture_criticism" title="Architecture criticism">architecture periodicals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LibraryPR_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LibraryPR-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> The library system participates with 15 other universities in digitizing its collections as a part of the <a href="/wiki/Google_Book_Search" title="Google Book Search" class="mw-redirect">Google Book Search</a> project.<sup id="cite_ref-LibraryPR_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LibraryPR-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mary_and_Leigh_Block_Museum_of_Art" title="Mary and Leigh Block Museum of Art">Mary and Leigh Block Museum of Art</a> is a major <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_museums_and_cultural_institutions_in_Chicago-area&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="List of museums and cultural institutions in Chicago-area (page does not exist)">art museum in Chicago</a>, containing more than 4,000 works in its permanent collection as well as dedicating a third of its space to temporary and traveling exhibitions.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_Educational_Foundation" title="Holocaust Educational Foundation">Holocaust Educational Foundation</a>, which had previously endowed the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Theodore_Zev_Weiss&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Theodore Zev Weiss (page does not exist)">Theodore Zev Weiss</a> ? Holocaust Educational Foundation Professorship in Holocaust Studies, became part of Northwestern.<sup id="cite_ref-NWHF_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NWHF-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HF_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HF-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg/220px-Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg/330px-Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg/440px-Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ford_Design_Building_Northwestern.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Ford Motor Company Engineering Design Center (2005)
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Northwestern was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> in 1917 and remains a research university with &quot;very high&quot; research activity.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AAU_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AAU-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Northwestern's schools of management, engineering, and communication are among the most academically productive in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-FSPI_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FSPI-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Northwestern received $511.7 million in research funding in 2011. Northwestern supports nearly 1,500 research laboratories across two campuses, predominately in the medical and biological sciences. Northwestern researchers disclosed 165 inventions, filed 76 patents applications, received 58 patents, started 4 companies, and generated $824.4 million in license income in 2009. The bulk of revenue has come from a patent on pregabalin, a synthesized organic molecule discovered by chemistry professor <a href="/wiki/Richard_Bruce_Silverman" title="Richard Bruce Silverman">Richard Silverman</a>, which ultimately was marketed as <a href="/wiki/Lyrica" title="Lyrica" class="mw-redirect">Lyrica</a>, a drug sold by <a href="/wiki/Pfizer" title="Pfizer">Pfizer</a>, to combat epilepsy, neuropathic pain, and fibromyalgia. The Lyrica returns in 2008 pushed Northwestern into first place among universities in licensing income.</p> 
     <p>Northwestern is home to the Center for Interdisciplinary Exploration and Research in Astrophysics, Northwestern Institute for Complex Systems, Nanoscale Science and Engineering Center, Materials Research Center, Institute for Policy Research, International Institute for Nanotechnology, Center for Catalysis and Surface Science, Buffet Center for International and Comparative Studies, the Initiative for Sustainability and Energy at Northwestern <sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Argonne/Northwestern_Solar_Energy_Research_Center" title="Argonne/Northwestern Solar Energy Research Center">Argonne/Northwestern Solar Energy Research Center</a> and other centers for interdisciplinary research.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_life">Campus life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Campus life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg/220px-Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg/330px-Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/17/Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg/440px-Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Northwestern_Rock_and_University_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Rock in front of University Hall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The undergraduates have a number of traditions: Painting <a href="/wiki/The_Rock_(Northwestern_University)" title="The Rock (Northwestern University)">The Rock</a> (originally a fountain donated by the Class of 1902) is a way to advertise, for example, campus organizations, events in Greek life, student groups, and university-wide events.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Dance_Marathon" title="Northwestern University Dance Marathon">Dance Marathon</a>, a 30-hour philanthropic event, has raised more than 13 million dollars in its history for various children's charities.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Primal Scream</i> is held at 9 p.m. on the Sunday before finals week every quarter; students lean out of windows or gather in courtyards and scream.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Armadillo Day, or, more popularly, <a href="/wiki/Dillo_Day" title="Dillo Day">Dillo Day</a>, is held on Northwestern's <a href="/wiki/Lakefill" title="Lakefill" class="mw-redirect">Lakefill</a> every Spring on the weekend after <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Day" title="Memorial Day">Memorial Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, every year during their freshman orientation, known as &quot;Welcome Week&quot;, the incoming freshman and transfer students perform the &quot;March Thru the Arch&quot;. This arch is famous at Northwestern, and it is located on the south end of their Evanston campus. This rite of passage is used to symbolize that all students at Northwestern are part of &quot;One Northwestern&quot;.</p> 
     <p>There are traditions long associated with football games. Students growl like wildcats when the opposing team controls the ball, while simulating a paw with their hands. They will also jingle keys at the beginning of each kickoff. In the past, before the tradition was discontinued, students would throw marshmallows during games.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The Clock Tower at the Rebecca Crown Center glows purple, instead of its usual white, after a winning game, thereby proclaiming the happy news. The Clock Tower remains purple until a loss or until the end of the sports season. Whereas formerly the Clock Tower was lighted only for football victories, wins for men's basketball and women's lacrosse now merit commemoration as well; important victories in other sports may also prompt an empurpling.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Northwestern" title="The Daily Northwestern">The Daily Northwestern</a></i> is the main student newspaper. Established in 1881, and published on weekdays during the academic year, it is directed entirely by undergraduates. Although it serves the Northwestern community, the <i>Daily</i> has no business ties to the university, being supported wholly by advertisers. It is owned by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Students_Publishing_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Students Publishing Company (page does not exist)">Students Publishing Company</a>. Current circulation is in excess of 7,500.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://politicsandpolicy.org/">Politics &amp; Policy</a> was founded at Northwestern and is dedicated to the analysis of current events and public policy. Begun in 2010 by students in the Weinberg College, School of Communication, and Medill School, the organization reaches students on more than two hundred and fifty college campuses around the world. Run entirely by undergraduates, Politics &amp; Policy publishes several times a week with material ranging from short summaries of events to extended research pieces. The organization is funded in part by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cics.northwestern.edu/">Buffett Center</a>.</p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/North_by_Northwestern" title="North by Northwestern">North by Northwestern</a></i> is an online undergraduate magazine, having been established in September 2006 by students at the Medill School. It's published on weekdays, with updates on news stories and special events inserted throughout the day and on weekends. <i>North by Northwestern</i> also publishes a quarterly print magazine, recently honored by the Society of Professional Journalists as the nation's best student magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/WNUR" title="WNUR" class="mw-redirect">WNUR</a> (89.3 <a href="/wiki/FM_radio" title="FM radio" class="mw-redirect">FM</a>) is a 7,200 watt <a href="/wiki/Radio_station" title="Radio station" class="mw-redirect">radio station</a> that broadcasts to Chicago and its northern suburbs. WNUR's programming consists of music ? jazz, classical, rock ? varsity sports (football, men's and women's basketball, baseball, softball, and women's lacrosse), breaking news on weekdays, politics, current events, and literature.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p><i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://northwesternbusinessreview.org/">Northwestern Business Review</a></i> is an online business publication. Founded in 2005, <i>Northwestern Business Review</i> has moved to a strictly online format.</p> 
     <p><i>Syllabus</i> is the undergraduate yearbook. First published in 1885, the yearbook is an epitome of that year's events at Northwestern. Published by Students Publishing Company and edited by Northwestern students, it is distributed in late May.</p> 
     <p><i>Northwestern Flipside</i> is an undergraduate satirical magazine. Founded in 2009, <i>The Flipside</i> publishes a weekly issue both in print and online.</p> 
     <p><i>Helicon</i> is the university's undergraduate literary magazine. Started in 1979, it is published twice a year, a web issue in the Winter, and a print issue with a web complement in the Spring.</p> 
     <p><i>TriQuarterly Online</i> (formerly TriQuarterly) is a literary magazine published twice a year featuring poetry, fiction, nonfiction, drama, literary essays, reviews, a blog, and graphic art. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://triquarterly.org/">[3]</a></p> 
     <p><i>Studio 22</i> is Northwestern's student-run production company which produces roughly ten films per year. The organization, for example, financed the first film Zach Braff directed and has produced many films in which students who would go on to successful acting careers performed, including Zach Gilford of the TV show, Friday Night Lights. <sup id="cite_ref-IMDB_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMDB-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i>Northwestern News Network</i> is the student television news and sports network at Northwestern University, serving the Northwestern and <a href="/wiki/Evanston,_Illinois" title="Evanston, Illinois">Evanston</a> communities. Its studios and newsroom are located on the fourth floor of the McCormick Tribune Center on Northwestern's Evanston campus. NNN is funded by the <a href="/wiki/Medill_School_of_Journalism" title="Medill School of Journalism">Medill School of Journalism</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Performing arts">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Two annual productions are especially notable: the Waa-Mu show, and the <a href="/wiki/Dolphin_show" title="Dolphin show" class="mw-redirect">Dolphin show</a>. Waa-Mu is an original musical, written and produced almost entirely by students.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Children's theater is represented on campus by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Griffin%27s_Tale&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Griffin's Tale (page does not exist)">Griffin's Tale</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Purple_Crayon_Players&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Purple Crayon Players (page does not exist)">Purple Crayon Players</a>.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Its umbrella organization?the Student Theatre Coalition, or StuCo?organizes nine student theatre companies, plus some other performance groups.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Students produce more than sixty independent productions each year.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many Northwestern alumni have used these productions as stepping stones to successful television and film careers. Chicago's Lookingglass Theatre, for example, which began life in the Great Room in <a href="/wiki/Jones_Residential_College" title="Jones Residential College" class="mw-redirect">Jones Residential College</a>, was founded in 1988 by several alumni, including <a href="/wiki/David_Schwimmer" title="David Schwimmer">David Schwimmer</a>; in 2011, it won the Regional Tony Award.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>Northwestern also has a variety of improv groups. The improv and sketch comedy group <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mee-Ow&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mee-Ow (page does not exist)">Mee-Ow</a> created by Paul Warshauer and Josh Lazar in 1974 lists <a href="/wiki/Julia_Louis-Dreyfus" title="Julia Louis-Dreyfus">Julia Louis-Dreyfus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ana_Gasteyer" title="Ana Gasteyer">Ana Gasteyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dermot_Mulroney" title="Dermot Mulroney">Dermot Mulroney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seth_Meyers" title="Seth Meyers">Seth Meyers</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Cameron_Mitchell" title="John Cameron Mitchell">John Cameron Mitchell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kristen_Schaal" title="Kristen Schaal">Kristen Schaal</a> among its alumni. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mee-Ow&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mee-Ow (page does not exist)">Mee-Ow</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.thetitanicplayers.com/">The Titanic Players</a>, and Out da Box, a multicultural comedy show, together with Northwestern's theatre department, have brought attention to Northwestern's improv comedy training and performance.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>The undergraduate students maintain twelve a cappella groups, including the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Undertones" title="Northwestern Undertones">Northwestern Undertones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Purple_Haze_(a_cappella_group)" title="Purple Haze (a cappella group)">Purple Haze</a>, and a variety of dance companies. The dance companies include Fusion Dance Company, Northwestern's premiere Hip-Hop Dance Crew; ReFresH Dance Crew, an open dance community that offers free hip-hop choreography and freestyling lessons;<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Graffiti Dancers, a dance group that focuses on jazz and modern; and Boomshaka, Northwestern's premiere drum and dance ensemble, combining body rhythm, drumming, and dance.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Radio drama featuring student voice actors is a staple of WNUR's programming.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Debate_Society">Debate Society</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Debate Society">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <i>Northwestern Debate Society</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Policy_debate" title="Policy debate">policy debate</a> team which has won fourteen <a href="/wiki/National_Debate_Tournament" title="National Debate Tournament">National Debate Tournaments</a>, the highest number of any university. Famous alumni of the Society include <a href="/wiki/Erwin_Chemerinsky" title="Erwin Chemerinsky">Erwin Chemerinsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elliot_Mincberg" title="Elliot Mincberg">Elliot Mincberg</a>, the latter senior vice president, general counsel and legal director of <a href="/wiki/People_For_the_American_Way" title="People For the American Way">People For the American Way</a>. Scott Deatherage, the head coach, was named the <i>Coach of the Nineties</i>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Service">Service</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Service">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Many students are involved in community service in one form or another. Annual events include <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Dance_Marathon" title="Northwestern University Dance Marathon">Dance Marathon</a>, a thirty-hour event that raised more than a million dollars for charity in 2011;<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> and Project Pumpkin, a <a href="/wiki/Halloween" title="Halloween">Halloween</a> celebration hosted by the Northwestern Community Development Corps (NCDC) to which more than 800 local children are invited for an afternoon of games and sweets. NCDC's work is to connect hundreds of student volunteers to some twenty volunteer sites in Evanston and Chicago throughout the year.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Many students have assisted with the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a> and have taken <a href="/wiki/Alternative_break" title="Alternative break">alternative spring break</a> trips to hundreds of service sites across the United States.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Northwestern students also participate in the Freshman Urban Program, a program for students interested in community service.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A large and growing number of students participate in the university's Global Engagement Summer Institute (GESI), a group service-learning expedition in Asia, Africa, or Latin America, in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/Foundation_for_Sustainable_Development" title="Foundation for Sustainable Development">Foundation for Sustainable Development</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Several internationally recognized <a href="/wiki/International_nongovernmental_organization" title="International nongovernmental organization">non-profit organizations</a> have originated at Northwestern including the <a href="/wiki/WHIA" title="WHIA" class="mw-redirect">World Health Imaging, Informatics and Telemedicine Alliance</a>, a spin-off from an engineering student's <a href="/wiki/Honors_course" title="Honors course" class="mw-redirect">honors</a> <a href="/wiki/Thesis" title="Thesis">thesis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate_housing">Undergraduate housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Undergraduate housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_residences" title="List of Northwestern University residences">List of Northwestern University residences</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Northwestern has several housing options, including both traditional residence halls and residential colleges which gather together students who have a particular intellectual interest in common. Among the residential colleges are the Residential College of Cultural and Community Studies (CCS), Ayers College of Commerce and Industry, Jones Residential College (Arts), Slivka Residential College (Science and Engineering), the International Studies Residential College, Communications Residential College (CRC), and the Public Affairs Residential College (PARC). Dorms include 1835 Hinman, Bobb-McCullough, Foster-Walker complex (commonly referred to as Plex), and several more. In Winter 2013, 39% of undergraduates were affiliated with a <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternity</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sorority" title="Sorority" class="mw-redirect">sorority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Northwestern recognizes 21 fraternities and 18 sororities.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats" title="Northwestern Wildcats">Northwestern Wildcats</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Lacrosse_women.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Lacrosse_women.jpg/170px-Lacrosse_women.jpg" width="170" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Lacrosse_women.jpg/255px-Lacrosse_women.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Lacrosse_women.jpg/340px-Lacrosse_women.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Lacrosse_women.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 2005 
        <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship" title="NCAA Women's Lacrosse Championship" class="mw-redirect">NCAA Women's Lacrosse Championship</a> game between the 
        <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers" title="Virginia Cavaliers">Virginia Cavaliers</a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats" title="Northwestern Wildcats">Northwestern Wildcats</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Northwestern is a charter member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> and the only private institution in the conference. Northwestern fields 19 intercollegiate athletic teams (8 men's and 11 women's) in addition to numerous club sports.<sup id="cite_ref-NU_Facts_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NU_Facts-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_women%27s_lacrosse" title="Northwestern Wildcats women's lacrosse">women's lacrosse team</a> won five consecutive <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Lacrosse_Championship" title="NCAA Women's Lacrosse Championship" class="mw-redirect">national championships</a> between 2005 and 2009, went undefeated in 2005 and 2009, added more NCAA championships in 2011 and 2012, giving them 7 NCAA championships in 8 years, and holds several scoring records.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The men's <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> team is recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Helms_Athletic_Foundation" title="Helms Athletic Foundation">Helms Athletic Foundation</a> as the 1931 National Champion.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2010?11 school year, the Wildcats had one national championship, 12 teams in postseason play, 20 All-Americans, two CoSIDA Academic All-American selections, 8 CoSIDA Academic All0District selections, 1 conference Coach of the Year and Player of the Year, 53 All-Conference and a record 201 Academic All-Big Ten athletes. Overall, 12 of Northwestern's 19 varsity programs had NCAA or bowl postseason appearances.</p> 
     <p>The football team plays at <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Field_(stadium)" title="Ryan Field (stadium)">Ryan Field</a> (formerly known as Dyche Stadium); the basketball and volleyball teams play at <a href="/wiki/Welsh-Ryan_Arena" title="Welsh-Ryan Arena">Welsh-Ryan Arena</a>. Northwestern's athletic teams are nicknamed the Wildcats. Before 1924, they were known as &quot;The Purple&quot; and unofficially as &quot;The Fighting Methodists.&quot; The name Wildcats was bestowed upon the university in 1924 by Wallace Abbey, a writer for the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Daily_Tribune" title="Chicago Daily Tribune" class="mw-redirect">Chicago Daily Tribune</a> who wrote that even in a loss to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>, &quot;Football players had not come down from Evanston; wildcats would be a name better suited to [Coach Glenn] <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Thistlethwaite" title="Glenn Thistlethwaite">Thistletwaite's</a> boys.&quot; <sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> The name was so popular that university board members made &quot;wildcats&quot; the official nickname just months later. In 1972, the student body voted to change the official nickname from &quot;Wildcats&quot; to &quot;Purple Haze&quot; but the new name never stuck.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The mascot of Northwestern Athletics is <a href="/wiki/Northwestern%27s_Willie_the_Wildcat" title="Northwestern's Willie the Wildcat" class="mw-redirect">Willie the Wildcat</a>. The first mascot, however, was a live, caged bear cub from the <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Park_Zoo" title="Lincoln Park Zoo">Lincoln Park Zoo</a> named Furpaw who was brought to the playing field on the day of a game to greet the fans. But after a losing season, the team, deciding that Furpaw was to blame for its misfortune, banished him from campus forever. Willie the Wildcat made his debut in 1933 first as a logo, and then in three dimensions in 1947, when members of the Alpha Delta fraternity dressed as wildcats during a Homecoming Parade. The <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_Wildcat_Marching_Band" title="Northwestern University Wildcat Marching Band">Northwestern University Marching Band (NUMB)</a> performs at all home football games and leads cheers in the student section and performs the <a href="/wiki/Alma_Mater" title="Alma Mater" class="mw-redirect">Alma Mater</a> at the end of the game.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ryan_Field.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Ryan_Field.jpg/220px-Ryan_Field.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Ryan_Field.jpg/330px-Ryan_Field.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Ryan_Field.jpg/440px-Ryan_Field.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ryan_Field.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Field_(stadium)" title="Ryan Field (stadium)">Ryan Field (1926)</a>, Northwestern's 49,000 seat football stadium
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_football" title="Northwestern Wildcats football">Northwestern's football team</a> has made 73 appearances in the top 10 of the AP poll since 1936 (including 5 at #1) and has won eight Big Ten conference championships since 1903.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-National_Champs_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Champs-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> At one time, Northwestern had the longest losing streak in Division I-A, losing 34 consecutive games between 1979 and 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Streak_ends_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Streak_ends-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> They did not appear in a bowl game after 1949 until the <a href="/wiki/1996_Rose_Bowl" title="1996 Rose Bowl">1996 Rose Bowl</a>. The team did not win a bowl since the <a href="/wiki/1949_Rose_Bowl" title="1949 Rose Bowl">1949 Rose Bowl</a> until the <a href="/wiki/2013_Gator_Bowl" title="2013 Gator Bowl">2013 Gator Bowl</a>. Following the sudden death of football coach <a href="/wiki/Randy_Walker_(football_coach)" title="Randy Walker (football coach)" class="mw-redirect">Randy Walker</a> in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> 31-year-old former <a href="/wiki/All-American" title="All-American" class="mw-redirect">All-American</a> Northwestern <a href="/wiki/Linebacker" title="Linebacker">linebacker</a> <a href="/wiki/Pat_Fitzgerald" title="Pat Fitzgerald">Pat Fitzgerald</a> assumed the position, becoming the youngest <a href="/wiki/List_of_current_NCAA_Division_I_FBS_football_coaches" title="List of current NCAA Division I FBS football coaches">Division I FBS coach</a> at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1998, two former <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball" title="Northwestern Wildcats men's basketball">Northwestern basketball</a> players were charged and convicted for sports bribery as a result of being paid to <a href="/wiki/Point_shaving" title="Point shaving">shave points</a> in games against three other Big Ten schools during the 1995 season.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Wildcats_football" title="Northwestern Wildcats football">football team</a> became embroiled in a different betting scandal later that year when federal prosecutors indicted four former players for perjury related to <a href="/wiki/Sports_betting" title="Sports betting">betting</a> on their own games.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2001, Rashidi Wheeler, a senior <a href="/wiki/Safety_(American_football_position)" title="Safety (American football position)" class="mw-redirect">safety</a>, collapsed and died during practice from an <a href="/wiki/Asthma_attack" title="Asthma attack" class="mw-redirect">asthma attack</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> An autopsy revealed that he had <a href="/wiki/Ephedrine" title="Ephedrine">ephedrine</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Stimulant" title="Stimulant">stimulant</a> banned by the <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a>, in his system, which prompted Northwestern to investigate the prevalence of stimulants and other banned substances across all of its athletic programs.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006, the Northwestern women's <a href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer" class="mw-redirect">soccer</a> team was suspended and coach Jenny Haigh resigned following the release of images of alleged <a href="/wiki/Hazing" title="Hazing">hazing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: People">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_body">Student body</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Student body">edit</a>]</span></h3>

     <p>Northwestern enrolled 8,367 full-time undergraduate and 8,108 full-time graduate and professional students in the 2010?11 academic year, along with approximately 1,100 part-time students.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS-B_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-B-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> The undergraduate population is drawn from all 50 states and over 100 foreign countries.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS-B_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-B-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> Admissions are characterized as &quot;more selective, lower transfer-in&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> There were over 32,000 applications for the undergraduate Class of 2017 (entering 2013): 13.9% were admitted.<sup id="cite_ref-Here.27s_to_the_Class_of_2017_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Here.27s_to_the_Class_of_2017-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Interquartile_range" title="Interquartile range">interquartile range</a> on the <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> was 1390?1550 (excluding the Writing Test) and 91% ranked in the top ten percent of their high school class.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS-C_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-C-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, Northwestern enrolled 249 <a href="/wiki/National_Merit_Scholars" title="National Merit Scholars" class="mw-redirect">National Merit Scholars</a> as freshmen, the third-largest total in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> 86% of students were graduated after four years, 92% after five years, the university having several five-year programs.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS-B_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-B-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty">Faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Faculty">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_faculty" title="List of Northwestern University faculty">List of Northwestern University faculty</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The university employs 2,291 full-time faculty members across its eleven schools,<sup id="cite_ref-Northwestern_Data_Book_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Northwestern_Data_Book-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> including 18 members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> 65 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> 19 members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> and 6 members of the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable faculty include 2010 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>- winning economist <a href="/wiki/Dale_T._Mortensen" title="Dale T. Mortensen">Dale T. Mortensen</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> nano-scientist <a href="/wiki/Chad_Mirkin" title="Chad Mirkin">Chad Mirkin</a>; Tony Award-winning director <a href="/wiki/Mary_Zimmerman" title="Mary Zimmerman">Mary Zimmerman</a>; management expert <a href="/wiki/Philip_Kotler" title="Philip Kotler">Philip Kotler</a>; King Faisal International Prize in Science recipient Sir <a href="/wiki/Fraser_Stoddart" title="Fraser Stoddart">Fraser Stoddart</a>; <a href="/wiki/Steppenwolf_Theatre" title="Steppenwolf Theatre" class="mw-redirect">Steppenwolf Theatre</a> director <a href="/wiki/Anna_Shapiro" title="Anna Shapiro" class="mw-redirect">Anna Shapiro</a>; sexual psychologist <a href="/wiki/J._Michael_Bailey" title="J. Michael Bailey">J. Michael Bailey</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Holocaust_denier" title="Holocaust denier" class="mw-redirect">Holocaust denier</a> <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Butz" title="Arthur Butz">Arthur Butz</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Federalist_Society" title="Federalist Society">Federalist Society</a> co-founder <a href="/wiki/Steven_Calabresi" title="Steven Calabresi" class="mw-redirect">Steven Calabresi</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> former <a href="/wiki/Weatherman_(organization)" title="Weatherman (organization)" class="mw-redirect">Weatherman</a> <a href="/wiki/Bernardine_Rae_Dohrn" title="Bernardine Rae Dohrn" class="mw-redirect">Bernardine Rae Dohrn</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ethnographer" title="Ethnographer" class="mw-redirect">ethnographer</a> <a href="/wiki/Gary_Alan_Fine" title="Gary Alan Fine">Gary Alan Fine</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>-winning historian <a href="/wiki/Garry_Wills" title="Garry Wills">Garry Wills</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellowship" title="MacArthur Fellowship" class="mw-redirect">MacArthur Fellowship</a> recipients <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Dybek" title="Stuart Dybek">Stuart Dybek</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Richeson" title="Jennifer Richeson">Jennifer Richeson</a>. Notable former faculty include political advisor <a href="/wiki/David_Axelrod" title="David Axelrod">David Axelrod</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> artist <a href="/wiki/Ed_Paschke" title="Ed Paschke">Ed Paschke</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> writer <a href="/wiki/Charles_Newman_(author)" title="Charles Newman (author)">Charles Newman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>-winning chemist <a href="/wiki/John_Pople" title="John Pople">John Pople</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> and military sociologist and &quot;<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_ask,_don%27t_tell" title="Don't ask, don't tell">don't ask, don't tell</a>&quot; author <a href="/wiki/Charles_Moskos" title="Charles Moskos">Charles Moskos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Northwestern_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Northwestern_University_alumni" title="List of Northwestern University alumni">List of Northwestern University alumni</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg/170px-CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg" width="170" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg/255px-CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg/340px-CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:CharltonHestonCivilRightsMarch1963Retouched.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Charlton_Heston" title="Charlton Heston">Charlton Heston</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>-winning actor, 
        <a href="/wiki/National_Rifle_Association" title="National Rifle Association">National Rifle Association</a> President, B.S. '45
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Northwestern has roughly 225,000 alumni in all branches of business, government, law, science, education, medicine, media, and the performing arts. Among Northwestern's more notable alumni are U.S. Senator and presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/George_McGovern" title="George McGovern">George McGovern</a>, Nobel Prize-winning economist <a href="/wiki/George_J._Stigler" title="George J. Stigler" class="mw-redirect">George J. Stigler</a>, Nobel Prize-winning novelist <a href="/wiki/Saul_Bellow" title="Saul Bellow">Saul Bellow</a>, Pulitzer Prize-winning composer and diarist <a href="/wiki/Ned_Rorem" title="Ned Rorem">Ned Rorem</a>, the much-decorated composer <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hanson" title="Howard Hanson">Howard Hanson</a>, Deputy Prime Minister of <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> <a href="/wiki/Ali_Babacan" title="Ali Babacan">Ali Babacan</a>, the historian and novelist <a href="/wiki/Wilma_Dykeman" title="Wilma Dykeman">Wilma Dykeman</a>, and the founder of the presidential prayer breakfast <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Vereide" title="Abraham Vereide">Abraham Vereide</a>. U.S. Supreme Court Associate Justice <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Stevens" title="John Paul Stevens">John Paul Stevens</a>, Supreme Court Justice and Ambassador to the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Joseph_Goldberg" title="Arthur Joseph Goldberg" class="mw-redirect">Arthur Joseph Goldberg</a>, and Governor of Illinois and Democratic presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Adlai_Stevenson_II" title="Adlai Stevenson II">Adlai Stevenson</a> are among the graduates of the <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_School_of_Law" title="Northwestern University School of Law">Northwestern School of Law</a>. Many Northwestern alumni play or have played important roles in <a href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" title="Chicago, Illinois" class="mw-redirect">Chicago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, such as former Illinois governor and convicted felon <a href="/wiki/Rod_Blagojevich" title="Rod Blagojevich">Rod Blagojevich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bulls" title="Chicago Bulls">Chicago Bulls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> owner <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Reinsdorf" title="Jerry Reinsdorf">Jerry Reinsdorf</a>, and theater director <a href="/wiki/Mary_Zimmerman" title="Mary Zimmerman">Mary Zimmerman</a>. Northwestern alumnus <a href="/wiki/David_J._Skorton" title="David J. Skorton">David J. Skorton</a> currently serves as president of <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rahm_Emanuel" title="Rahm Emanuel">Rahm Emanuel</a>, the mayor of Chicago and former <a href="/wiki/White_House_Chief_of_Staff" title="White House Chief of Staff">White House Chief of Staff</a>, earned a Masters in Speech and Communication in 1985.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:John_Paul_Stevens,_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/John_Paul_Stevens%2C_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg/170px-John_Paul_Stevens%2C_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg" width="170" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/John_Paul_Stevens%2C_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg/255px-John_Paul_Stevens%2C_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3b/John_Paul_Stevens%2C_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:John_Paul_Stevens,_SCOTUS_photo_portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Stevens" title="John Paul Stevens">John Paul Stevens</a>, 
        <a href="/wiki/Associate_Justice_of_the_United_States_Supreme_Court" title="Associate Justice of the United States Supreme Court" class="mw-redirect">Associate Justice of the United States Supreme Court</a>, J.D. '47
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Northwestern's School of Communication has been especially fruitful in the number of actors, actresses, playwrights, and film and television writers and directors it has produced. Alumni who have made their mark on film and television include <a href="/wiki/Ann-Margret" title="Ann-Margret">Ann-Margret</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warren_Beatty" title="Warren Beatty">Warren Beatty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Lynde" title="Paul Lynde">Paul Lynde</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Schwimmer" title="David Schwimmer">David Schwimmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anne_Dudek" title="Anne Dudek">Anne Dudek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zach_Braff" title="Zach Braff">Zach Braff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zooey_Deschanel" title="Zooey Deschanel">Zooey Deschanel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marg_Helgenberger" title="Marg Helgenberger">Marg Helgenberger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julia_Louis-Dreyfus" title="Julia Louis-Dreyfus">Julia Louis-Dreyfus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Orbach" title="Jerry Orbach">Jerry Orbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Jones" title="Jennifer Jones">Jennifer Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Springer" title="Jerry Springer">Jerry Springer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Megan_Mullally" title="Megan Mullally">Megan Mullally</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Cameron_Mitchell" title="John Cameron Mitchell">John Cameron Mitchell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dermot_Mulroney" title="Dermot Mulroney">Dermot Mulroney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlton_Heston" title="Charlton Heston">Charlton Heston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Kind" title="Richard Kind">Richard Kind</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ana_Gasteyer" title="Ana Gasteyer">Ana Gasteyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brad_Hall" title="Brad Hall">Brad Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shelley_Long" title="Shelley Long">Shelley Long</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Daniels" title="William Daniels">William Daniels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cloris_Leachman" title="Cloris Leachman">Cloris Leachman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Bartlett" title="Bonnie Bartlett">Bonnie Bartlett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paula_Prentiss" title="Paula Prentiss">Paula Prentiss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Benjamin" title="Richard Benjamin">Richard Benjamin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laura_Innes" title="Laura Innes">Laura Innes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Busch" title="Charles Busch">Charles Busch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_March" title="Stephanie March">Stephanie March</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Roberts_(actor)" title="Tony Roberts (actor)">Tony Roberts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeri_Ryan" title="Jeri Ryan">Jeri Ryan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kimberly_Williams-Paisley" title="Kimberly Williams-Paisley">Kimberly Williams-Paisley</a>, <a href="/wiki/McLean_Stevenson" title="McLean Stevenson">McLean Stevenson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Randall" title="Tony Randall">Tony Randall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Rae" title="Charlotte Rae">Charlotte Rae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Neal" title="Patricia Neal">Patricia Neal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Dussault" title="Nancy Dussault">Nancy Dussault</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Reed" title="Robert Reed">Robert Reed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mara_Brock_Akil" title="Mara Brock Akil">Mara Brock Akil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greg_Berlanti" title="Greg Berlanti">Greg Berlanti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Shor" title="Dan Shor">Dan Shor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seth_Meyers" title="Seth Meyers">Seth Meyers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_DeCaro" title="Frank DeCaro">Frank DeCaro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zach_Gilford" title="Zach Gilford">Zach Gilford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Sullivan" title="Nicole Sullivan">Nicole Sullivan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Colbert" title="Stephen Colbert">Stephen Colbert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Garry_Marshall" title="Garry Marshall">Garry Marshall</a>. Directors who were graduated from Northwestern include <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Freedman" title="Gerald Freedman">Gerald Freedman</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stuart_Hagmann&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stuart Hagmann (page does not exist)">Stuart Hagmann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_W._Mason" title="Marshall W. Mason">Marshall W. Mason</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mary_Zimmerman" title="Mary Zimmerman">Mary Zimmerman</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lee_Phillip_Bell" title="Lee Phillip Bell">Lee Phillip Bell</a> hosted a talk show in Chicago from 1952 to 1986 and co-created the <a href="/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award" title="Daytime Emmy Award">Daytime Emmy Award</a>-winning soap operas <i><a href="/wiki/The_Young_and_the_Restless" title="The Young and the Restless">The Young and the Restless</a></i> in 1973 and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bold_and_the_Beautiful" title="The Bold and the Beautiful">The Bold and the Beautiful</a></i> in 1987. Alumni such as <a href="/wiki/Sheldon_Harnick" title="Sheldon Harnick">Sheldon Harnick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_D%27Abruzzo" title="Stephanie D'Abruzzo">Stephanie D'Abruzzo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heather_Headley" title="Heather Headley">Heather Headley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kristen_Schaal" title="Kristen Schaal">Kristen Schaal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lily_Rabe" title="Lily Rabe">Lily Rabe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Walter_Kerr" title="Walter Kerr">Walter Kerr</a> have distinguished themselves on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theater" title="Broadway theater" class="mw-redirect">Broadway</a>, as has designer <a href="/wiki/Bob_Mackie" title="Bob Mackie">Bob Mackie</a>. Amsterdam-based comedy theater <a href="/wiki/Boom_Chicago" title="Boom Chicago">Boom Chicago</a> was founded by Northwestern alumni, and the school has become a training ground for future <a href="/wiki/The_Second_City" title="The Second City">The Second City</a>, <a href="/wiki/I.O." title="I.O." class="mw-redirect">I.O.</a>, <a href="/wiki/ComedySportz" title="ComedySportz">ComedySportz</a>, <a href="/wiki/MADtv" title="MADtv">Mad TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a> talent.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tam_Spiva" title="Tam Spiva">Tam Spiva</a> wrote scripts for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Brady_Bunch" title="The Brady Bunch">The Brady Bunch</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Gentle_Ben" title="Gentle Ben">Gentle Ben</a></i>. In New York, Los Angeles, and Chicago, the number of Northwestern alumni involved in theater, film, and television is so large that a perception has formed that there's such a thing as a &quot;Northwestern mafia.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Medill_School_of_Journalism" title="Medill School of Journalism">Medill School of Journalism</a> has produced notable journalists and political activists including 38 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> laureates. National correspondents, reporters and columnists such as <i>The New York Times'</i>s <a href="/wiki/Elisabeth_Bumiller" title="Elisabeth Bumiller">Elisabeth Bumiller</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Barstow" title="David Barstow">David Barstow</a>, Dean Murphy, and <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Laforet" title="Vincent Laforet">Vincent Laforet</a>, <a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a>'s Gary Levin, <a href="/wiki/Susan_Page" title="Susan Page">Susan Page</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christine_Brennan" title="Christine Brennan">Christine Brennan</a>, <a href="/wiki/NBC_News" title="NBC News">NBC</a> correspondent <a href="/wiki/Kelly_O%27Donnell" title="Kelly O'Donnell">Kelly O'Donnell</a>, <a href="/wiki/CBS_News" title="CBS News">CBS</a> correspondent <a href="/wiki/Richard_Threlkeld" title="Richard Threlkeld">Richard Threlkeld</a>, <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> correspondents <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Lapin" title="Nicole Lapin">Nicole Lapin</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Joie_Chen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Joie Chen (page does not exist)">Joie Chen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> personalities <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Nichols_(reporter)" title="Rachel Nichols (reporter)" class="mw-redirect">Rachel Nichols</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Wilbon" title="Michael Wilbon">Michael Wilbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Greenberg" title="Mike Greenberg">Mike Greenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Weissman" title="Steve Weissman">Steve Weissman</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._A._Adande" title="J. A. Adande">J. A. Adande</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Blackistone" title="Kevin Blackistone">Kevin Blackistone</a>. The bestselling author of the <a href="/wiki/A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire" title="A Song of Ice and Fire">A Song of Ice and Fire</a> series, <a href="/wiki/George_R._R._Martin" title="George R. R. Martin">George R. R. Martin</a>, earned a B.S. and M.S. from Medill.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Northwestern_Magazine_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Northwestern_Magazine-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Feinberg School of Medicine (previously the Northwestern University Medical School) has produced a number of notable graduates, including Mary Harris Thompson, Class of 1870, ad eundem, first female surgeon in Chicago, first female surgeon at Cook County Hospital, and founder of the Mary Thomson Hospital, Roswell Park, Class of 1876, prominent surgeon for whom the Roswell Park Cancer Institute in Buffalo, NY, is named, Daniel Hale Williams, Class of 1883, performed the first successful American open heart surgery; only black charter member of the American College of Surgeons, Charles Horace Mayo, Class of 1888, co-founder of Mayo Clinic, Carlos Montezuma, Class of 1889, one of the first Native Americans to receive a Doctor of Medicine degree from any school, and founder of the Society of American Indians, Howard T. Ricketts, Class of 1897, who discovered bacteria of the genus Rickettsia, and identified the cause and methods of transmission of rocky mountain spotted fever, Allen B. Kanavel, Class of 1899, founder, regent, and president of the American College of Surgeons, internationally recognized as founder of modern hand and peripheral nerve surgery, Robert F. Furchgott, Class of 1940, received a Lasker Award in 1996 and the 1998 Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine for his co-discovery of nitric oxide, Thomas E. Starzl, Class of 1952, performed the first successful liver transplant in 1967 and received the National Medal of Science in 2004 and a Lasker Award in 2012, Joseph P. Kerwin, first physician in space, flew on three skylab missions and later served as director of Space and Life Sciences at NASA, C. Richard Schlegel, Class of 1972, developed the dominant patent for a vaccine against human papillomavirus (HPV) (administered as Gardasil) to prevent cervical cancer, David J. Skorton, Class of 1974, a noted cardiologist became president of Cornell University in 2006, and Andrew E. Senyei, Class of 1979, inventor, venture capitalist, and entrepreneur, founder of biotech and genetics companies, and a university trustee.</p> 
     <p>Northwestern alumni involved in music include <a href="/wiki/Steve_Albini" title="Steve Albini">Steve Albini</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Tyra" title="Thomas Tyra">Thomas Tyra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bird" title="Andrew Bird">Andrew Bird</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Radin" title="Joshua Radin">Joshua Radin</a>, members of <a href="/wiki/Arcade_Fire" title="Arcade Fire">Arcade Fire</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Lawrence_Arms" title="The Lawrence Arms">The Lawrence Arms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chavez_(band)" title="Chavez (band)">Chavez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dawen" title="Dawen">Dawen</a>, and <a href="/wiki/OK_Go" title="OK Go">OK Go</a>. Lastly, Northwestern alumni involved in professional sports include <a href="/wiki/Rick_Sund" title="Rick Sund">Rick Sund</a> (NBA), <a href="/wiki/Billy_McKinney_(basketball)" title="Billy McKinney (basketball)">Billy McKinney</a> (NBA), <a href="/wiki/Mark_Loretta" title="Mark Loretta">Mark Loretta</a> (MLB), <a href="/wiki/Joe_Girardi" title="Joe Girardi">Joe Girardi</a> (MLB), <a href="/wiki/Luis_Castillo_(American_football)" title="Luis Castillo (American football)">Luis Castillo</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Adams_(American_football)" title="Ernie Adams (American football)">Ernie Adams</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Otto_Graham" title="Otto Graham">Otto Graham</a> (NFL), <a href="/wiki/Mike_Kafka" title="Mike Kafka">Mike Kafka</a> (NFL), six-time Olympic medalist <a href="/wiki/Matt_Grevers" title="Matt Grevers">Matt Grevers</a>, and PGA Tour star <a href="/wiki/Luke_Donald" title="Luke Donald">Luke Donald</a>.</p>

       <li id="cite_note-Northwestern-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Northwestern_12-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.northwestern.edu/magazine/northwestern/summer2002/features/coverstory/index.htm">&quot;Keeping the Faith&quot;</a>. Northwestern<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved 2007-07-20</span>. &quot;Northwestern's own religious identity stretches back to its genesis. The University began with a prayer ? the school's nine founders (all of them Methodists, three of them ministers) knelt in worship before launching their first organizational meeting. During that meeting, they agreed to establish a university under the patronage of the Methodist Episcopal Church. Through most of its history, Northwestern kept a strong Methodist tie. Regional church conferences chose a member of the board of trustees, and until 1890 every University president was an ordained Methodist minister.&quot;</span><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANorthwestern+University&amp;rft.btitle=Keeping+the+Faith&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.northwestern.edu%2Fmagazine%2Fnorthwestern%2Fsummer2002%2Ffeatures%2Fcoverstory%2Findex.htm&amp;rft.pub=Northwestern&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span></span></li>
